   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">

   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of unsolved problems in physics
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <p>
       Some of the major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_unsolved_problems" title="List of unsolved problems">
        unsolved problems
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">
        physics
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Theory" title="Theory">
        theoretical
       </a>
       , meaning that existing theories seem incapable of explaining a certain observed
       <a href="/wiki/Phenomenon" title="Phenomenon">
        phenomenon
       </a>
       or experimental result. The others are
       <a href="/wiki/Experiment" title="Experiment">
        experimental
       </a>
       , meaning that there is a difficulty in creating an experiment to test a proposed theory or investigate a phenomenon in greater detail.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are still some deficiencies in the
       <a href="/wiki/Physics_beyond_the_Standard_Model" title="Physics beyond the Standard Model">
        Standard Model
       </a>
       of physics, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_mass" title="Origin of mass">
        origin of mass
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Strong_CP_problem" title="Strong CP problem">
        strong CP problem
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Neutrino_oscillation" title="Neutrino oscillation">
        neutrino oscillations
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matter%E2%80%93antimatter_asymmetry" title="Matter–antimatter asymmetry">
        matter–antimatter asymmetry
       </a>
       , and the nature of
       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">
        dark matter
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">
        dark energy
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sym-v2-feb-05_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sym-v2-feb-05-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Another problem lies within the
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">
        mathematical framework
       </a>
       of the Standard Model itself—the Standard Model is inconsistent with that of
       <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
        general relativity
       </a>
       , to the point that one or both theories break down under certain conditions (for example within known
       <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">
        spacetime
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_singularity" title="Gravitational singularity">
        singularities
       </a>
       like the
       <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">
        Big Bang
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_hole#Singularity" title="Black hole">
        centers
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">
        black holes
       </a>
       beyond the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Event_horizons" title="Event horizons">
        event horizon
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>
      <div class="toc" id="toc">
       <div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en">

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Unsolved_problems_by_subfield">
        Unsolved problems by subfield
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Unsolved problems by subfield">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The following is a list of unsolved problems grouped into broad areas of physics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="General_physics.2Fquantum_physics">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="General_physics/quantum_physics">
        General physics/quantum physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: General physics/quantum physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Arrow_of_time" title="Arrow of time">
         Arrow of time
        </a>
        (e.g.
        <a href="/wiki/Entropy_(arrow_of_time)" title="Entropy (arrow of time)">
         entropy's arrow of time
        </a>
        ): Why does
        <a href="/wiki/Arrow_of_time" title="Arrow of time">
         time have a direction
        </a>
        ? Why did the universe have such low
        <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">
         entropy
        </a>
        in the past, and time correlates with the universal (but not local) increase in entropy, from the past and to the future, according to the
        <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Second law of thermodynamics">
         second law of thermodynamics
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Why are
        <a href="/wiki/CP_violation" title="CP violation">
         CP violations
        </a>
        observed in certain weak force decays, but not elsewhere? Are CP violations somehow a product of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Law_of_Thermodynamics" title="Second Law of Thermodynamics">
         Second Law of Thermodynamics
        </a>
        , or are they a separate
        <a href="/wiki/Arrow_of_time" title="Arrow of time">
         arrow of time
        </a>
        ? Are there exceptions to the principle of
        <a href="/wiki/Causality_(physics)" title="Causality (physics)">
         causality
        </a>
        ? Is there a single possible past? Is the
        <a href="/wiki/Present#Philosophy_and_science" title="Present">
         present
        </a>
        moment physically distinct from the past and future, or is it merely an emergent property of
        <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">
         consciousness
        </a>
        ? What links the quantum arrow of time to the thermodynamic arrow?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interpretation_of_quantum_mechanics" title="Interpretation of quantum mechanics">
         Interpretation of quantum mechanics
        </a>
        : How does the quantum description of reality, which includes elements such as the
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_superposition" title="Quantum superposition">
         superposition
        </a>
        of states and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wavefunction_collapse" title="Wavefunction collapse">
         wavefunction collapse
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_decoherence" title="Quantum decoherence">
         quantum decoherence
        </a>
        , give rise to the reality we perceive?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Another way of stating this question regards the
        <a href="/wiki/Measurement_problem" title="Measurement problem">
         measurement problem
        </a>
        : What constitutes a "measurement" which apparently causes the wave function to collapse into a definite state? Unlike classical physical processes, some quantum mechanical processes (such as
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_teleportation" title="Quantum teleportation">
         quantum teleportation
        </a>
        arising from
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_entanglement" title="Quantum entanglement">
         quantum entanglement
        </a>
        ) cannot be simultaneously "local", "causal", and "real", but it is not obvious which of these properties must be sacrificed,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_5-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-:5-5">
          [5]
         </a>
        </sup>
        or if an attempt to describe
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Quantum_mechanical_processes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Quantum mechanical processes (page does not exist)">
         quantum mechanical processes
        </a>
        in these senses is a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Category_error" title="Category error">
         category error
        </a>
        such that a proper understanding of quantum mechanics would render the question meaningless.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Unification_Theory" title="Grand Unification Theory">
         Grand Unification Theory
        </a>
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_everything" title="Theory of everything">
         Theory of everything
        </a>
        : Is there a theory which explains the values of all
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamental_physical_constants" title="Fundamental physical constants">
         fundamental physical constants
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Is there a theory which explains why the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauge_group" title="Gauge group">
         gauge groups
        </a>
        of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_model" title="Standard model">
         standard model
        </a>
        are as they are, and why observed
        <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">
         spacetime
        </a>
        has 3 spatial dimensions and 1 temporal dimension? Do "fundamental physical constants" vary over time? Are any of the fundamental particles in the standard model of particle physics actually composite particles too tightly bound to observe as such at current experimental energies? Are there fundamental particles that have not yet been observed, and, if so, which ones are they and what are their properties? Are there
        <a href="/wiki/Fifth_force" title="Fifth force">
         unobserved fundamental forces
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Yang%E2%80%93Mills_theory" title="Yang–Mills theory">
         Yang–Mills theory
        </a>
        : Given an arbitrary
        <a href="/wiki/Compact_space" title="Compact space">
         compact
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauge_symmetry" title="Gauge symmetry">
         gauge group
        </a>
        , does a non-trivial quantum
        <a href="/wiki/Yang%E2%80%93Mills_theory" title="Yang–Mills theory">
         Yang–Mills theory
        </a>
        with a finite
        <a href="/wiki/Mass_gap" title="Mass gap">
         mass gap
        </a>
        exist? This problem is also listed as one of the
        <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Prize_Problems" title="Millennium Prize Problems">
         Millennium Prize Problems
        </a>
        in mathematics.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
         <a href="#cite_note-6">
          [6]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Physical_information" title="Physical information">
         Physical information
        </a>
        : Are there physical phenomena, such as
        <a href="/wiki/Wave_function_collapse" title="Wave function collapse">
         wave function collapse
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">
         black holes
        </a>
        , which irrevocably destroy information about their prior states?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_7-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-:2-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
        How is
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_information" title="Quantum information">
         quantum information
        </a>
        stored as a state of a quantum system?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dimensionless_physical_constant" title="Dimensionless physical constant">
         Dimensionless physical constant
        </a>
        : At the present time, the values of the dimensionless physical constants cannot be calculated; they are determined only by physical measurement.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
         <a href="#cite_note-8">
          [8]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Effelsberg_9-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Effelsberg-9">
          [9]
         </a>
        </sup>
        What is the minimum number of dimensionless physical constants from which all other dimensionless physical constants can be derived? Are dimensional physical constants necessary at all?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fine-tuned_Universe" title="Fine-tuned Universe">
         Fine-tuned Universe
        </a>
        : The values of the fundamental physical constants are in a narrow range necessary to support carbon-based life.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_10-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-:0-10">
          [10]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_11-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-:1-11">
          [11]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
         <a href="#cite_note-12">
          [12]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Is this because there exist
        <a href="/wiki/Multiverse" title="Multiverse">
         other universes
        </a>
        with different constants, or are our universe’s constants the result of chance, or some other factor or process?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">
         Quantum field theory
        </a>
        : Is it possible to construct, in the mathematically rigorous framework of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algebraic_quantum_field_theory" title="Algebraic quantum field theory">
         algebraic QFT
        </a>
        , a theory in 4-dimensional spacetime that includes interactions and does not resort to
        <a href="/wiki/Perturbation_theory_(quantum_mechanics)" title="Perturbation theory (quantum mechanics)">
         perturbative methods
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
         <a href="#cite_note-13">
          [13]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
         <a href="#cite_note-14">
          [14]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cosmology_and_general_relativity">
        Cosmology and general relativity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cosmology and general relativity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Problem_of_time" title="Problem of time">
         Problem of time
        </a>
        : In quantum mechanics time is a classical background parameter and the flow of time is universal and absolute. In general relativity time is one component of four-dimensional spacetime, and the flow of time changes depending on the curvature of spacetime and the spacetime trajectory of the observer. How can these two concepts of time be reconciled?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
         <a href="#cite_note-15">
          [15]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_inflation" title="Cosmic inflation">
         Cosmic inflation
        </a>
        : Is the theory of cosmic inflation correct, and, if so, what are the details of this epoch? What is the hypothetical
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inflaton_field" title="Inflaton field">
         inflaton field
        </a>
        giving rise to inflation? If inflation happened at one point, is it
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chaotic_inflation" title="Chaotic inflation">
         self-sustaining through inflation of quantum-mechanical fluctuations
        </a>
        , and thus ongoing in some extremely distant place?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-podolsky-NEQNET_16-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-podolsky-NEQNET-16">
          [16]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Horizon_problem" title="Horizon problem">
         Horizon problem
        </a>
        : Why is the distant universe so homogeneous when the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Bang_theory" title="Big Bang theory">
         Big Bang theory
        </a>
        seems to predict larger measurable
        <a href="/wiki/Anisotropy" title="Anisotropy">
         anisotropies
        </a>
        of the night sky than those observed? Cosmological
        <a href="/wiki/Inflation_(cosmology)" title="Inflation (cosmology)">
         inflation
        </a>
        is generally accepted as the solution, but are other possible explanations such as a
        <a href="/wiki/Variable_speed_of_light" title="Variable speed of light">
         variable speed of light
        </a>
        more appropriate?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newscientist_17-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-newscientist-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Why_is_there_something_rather_than_nothing%3F" title="Why is there something rather than nothing?">
         Origin
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_fate_of_the_universe" title="Ultimate fate of the universe">
         future of the universe
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang#Origin_of_conditions_required_for_Big_Bang_to_occur" title="Big Bang">
         How did the conditions for anything to exist arise?
        </a>
        Is the universe heading towards a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Freeze" title="Big Freeze">
         Big Freeze
        </a>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Rip" title="Big Rip">
         Big Rip
        </a>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Crunch" title="Big Crunch">
         Big Crunch
        </a>
        , or a
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Bounce" title="Big Bounce">
         Big Bounce
        </a>
        ? Or is it part of an infinitely recurring
        <a href="/wiki/Cyclic_model" title="Cyclic model">
         cyclic model
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Universe#Size_and_regions" title="Universe">
         Size of universe
        </a>
        : The diameter of the
        <a href="/wiki/Observable_universe" title="Observable universe">
         observable universe
        </a>
        is about 93 billion light-years, but what is the size of the whole universe? Does a
        <a href="/wiki/Multiverse" title="Multiverse">
         multiverse
        </a>
        exist?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Baryon_asymmetry" title="Baryon asymmetry">
         Baryon asymmetry
        </a>
        : Why is there far more
        <a href="/wiki/Matter" title="Matter">
         matter
        </a>
        than
        <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">
         antimatter
        </a>
        in the
        <a href="/wiki/Observable_universe" title="Observable universe">
         observable universe
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmological_constant_problem#Cosmological_constant_problem" title="Cosmological constant problem">
         Cosmological constant problem
        </a>
        : Why does the
        <a href="/wiki/Zero-point_energy" title="Zero-point energy">
         zero-point energy
        </a>
        of the
        <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">
         vacuum
        </a>
        not cause a large
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmological_constant" title="Cosmological constant">
         cosmological constant
        </a>
        ? What cancels it out?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
         <a href="#cite_note-18">
          [18]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_19-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-:3-19">
          [19]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DMPie_2013.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="341" data-file-width="341" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/DMPie_2013.svg/250px-DMPie_2013.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/DMPie_2013.svg/375px-DMPie_2013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/DMPie_2013.svg/500px-DMPie_2013.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DMPie_2013.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Estimated distribution of dark matter and dark energy in the universe
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">
         Dark matter
        </a>
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_rotation_curve" title="Galaxy rotation curve">
         Galaxy rotation curve
        </a>
        : What is the identity of dark matter?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newscientist_17-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-newscientist-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Is it a
        <a href="/wiki/Elementary_particle" title="Elementary particle">
         particle
        </a>
        ? Is it the lightest
        <a href="/wiki/Superpartner" title="Superpartner">
         superpartner
        </a>
        (LSP)? Or, do the
        <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_rotation_curve" title="Galaxy rotation curve">
         phenomena attributed to dark matter
        </a>
        point not to some form of matter but actually to an
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modified_models_of_gravity" title="Modified models of gravity">
         extension of gravity
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dark_energy" title="Dark energy">
         Dark energy
        </a>
        : What is the cause of the observed
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accelerated_expansion" title="Accelerated expansion">
         accelerated expansion
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/De_Sitter_universe" title="De Sitter universe">
         de Sitter phase
        </a>
        ) of the universe? Why is the energy density of the dark energy component of the same magnitude as the density of matter at present when the two evolve quite differently over time; could it be simply that we are observing at exactly the
        <a href="/wiki/Anthropic_principle" title="Anthropic principle">
         right time
        </a>
        ? Is dark energy a pure cosmological constant or are models of
        <a href="/wiki/Quintessence_(physics)" title="Quintessence (physics)">
         quintessence
        </a>
        such as
        <a href="/wiki/Phantom_energy" title="Phantom energy">
         phantom energy
        </a>
        applicable?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dark_flow" title="Dark flow">
         Dark flow
        </a>
        : Is a non-spherically symmetric gravitational pull from outside the observable universe responsible for some of the observed motion of large objects such as galactic clusters in the universe?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Axis_of_evil_(cosmology)" title="Axis of evil (cosmology)">
         Axis of evil (cosmology)
        </a>
        : Some large features of the microwave sky at distances of over 13 billion light years appear to be aligned with both the motion and orientation of the solar system. Is this due to systematic errors in processing, contamination of results by local effects, or an unexplained violation of the
        <a href="/wiki/Copernican_principle" title="Copernican principle">
         Copernican principle
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Shape_of_the_universe" title="Shape of the universe">
         Shape of the universe
        </a>
        : What is the 3-
        <a href="/wiki/Manifold" title="Manifold">
         manifold
        </a>
        of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comoving_coordinates" title="Comoving coordinates">
         comoving space
        </a>
        , i.e. of a comoving spatial section of the universe, informally called the "shape" of the universe? Neither the curvature nor the topology is presently known, though the curvature is known to be "close" to zero on observable scales. The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_inflation" title="Cosmic inflation">
         cosmic inflation
        </a>
        hypothesis suggests that the shape of the universe may be unmeasurable, but, since 2003,
        <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Luminet" title="Jean-Pierre Luminet">
         Jean-Pierre Luminet
        </a>
        , et al., and other groups have suggested that the shape of the universe may be the
        <a href="/wiki/Homology_sphere#Cosmology" title="Homology sphere">
         Poincaré dodecahedral space
        </a>
        . Is the shape unmeasurable; the Poincaré space; or another 3-manifold?
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Quantum_gravity">
        Quantum gravity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Quantum gravity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmological_constant_problem" title="Cosmological constant problem">
         Vacuum catastrophe
        </a>
        : Why does the predicted mass of the
        <a href="/wiki/Vacuum_state" title="Vacuum state">
         quantum vacuum
        </a>
        have little effect on the expansion of the universe?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_19-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-:3-19">
          [19]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_gravity" title="Quantum gravity">
         Quantum gravity
        </a>
        : Can
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">
         quantum mechanics
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
         general relativity
        </a>
        be realized as a fully consistent theory (perhaps as a
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_field_theory" title="Quantum field theory">
         quantum field theory
        </a>
        )?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
         <a href="#cite_note-20">
          [20]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Is spacetime fundamentally continuous or discrete? Would a consistent theory involve a force mediated by a hypothetical
        <a href="/wiki/Graviton" title="Graviton">
         graviton
        </a>
        , or be a product of a discrete structure of spacetime itself (as in
        <a href="/wiki/Loop_quantum_gravity" title="Loop quantum gravity">
         loop quantum gravity
        </a>
        )? Are there deviations from the predictions of general relativity at very small or very large scales or in other extreme circumstances that flow from a quantum gravity theory?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">
         Black holes
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Black_hole_information_paradox" title="Black hole information paradox">
         black hole information paradox
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_hole_radiation" title="Black hole radiation">
         black hole radiation
        </a>
        : Do black holes produce thermal radiation, as expected on theoretical grounds?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_7-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-:2-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Does this radiation contain information about their inner structure, as suggested by
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauge%E2%80%93gravity_duality" title="Gauge–gravity duality">
         gauge–gravity duality
        </a>
        , or not, as implied by
        <a href="/wiki/Hawking_radiation" title="Hawking radiation">
         Hawking
        </a>
        's original calculation? If not, and black holes can evaporate away, what happens to the information stored in them (since quantum mechanics does not provide for the destruction of information)? Or does the radiation stop at some point leaving black hole remnants? Is there another way to probe their internal structure somehow, if such a structure
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/No_hair_theorem" title="No hair theorem">
         even exists
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Extra_dimensions" title="Extra dimensions">
         Extra dimensions
        </a>
        : Does nature have more than four
        <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">
         spacetime
        </a>
        dimensions? If so, what is their size? Are dimensions a fundamental property of the universe or an emergent result of other physical laws? Can we experimentally observe evidence of higher spatial dimensions?
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_censorship_hypothesis" title="Cosmic censorship hypothesis">
         cosmic censorship hypothesis
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Chronology_protection_conjecture" title="Chronology protection conjecture">
         chronology protection conjecture
        </a>
        : Can singularities not hidden behind an event horizon, known as "
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naked_singularities" title="Naked singularities">
         naked singularities
        </a>
        ", arise from realistic initial conditions, or is it possible to prove some version of the "cosmic censorship hypothesis" of
        <a href="/wiki/Roger_Penrose" title="Roger Penrose">
         Roger Penrose
        </a>
        which proposes that this is impossible?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
         <a href="#cite_note-21">
          [21]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Similarly, will the
        <a href="/wiki/Closed_timelike_curve" title="Closed timelike curve">
         closed timelike curves
        </a>
        which arise in some solutions to the equations of general relativity (and which imply the possibility of backwards
        <a href="/wiki/Time_travel" title="Time travel">
         time travel
        </a>
        ) be ruled out by a theory of
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_gravity" title="Quantum gravity">
         quantum gravity
        </a>
        which unites general relativity with quantum mechanics, as suggested by the "chronology protection conjecture" of
        <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">
         Stephen Hawking
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Principle_of_locality" title="Principle of locality">
         Locality
        </a>
        : Are there non-local phenomena in quantum physics?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
         <a href="#cite_note-22">
          [22]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
         <a href="#cite_note-23">
          [23]
         </a>
        </sup>
        If they exist, are non-local phenomena limited to the entanglement revealed in the violations of the
        <a href="/wiki/Bell%27s_theorem" title="Bell's theorem">
         Bell inequalities
        </a>
        , or can information and conserved quantities also move in a non-local way? Under what circumstances are non-local phenomena observed? What does the existence or absence of non-local phenomena imply about the fundamental structure of spacetime? How does this relate to
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_entanglement" title="Quantum entanglement">
         quantum entanglement
        </a>
        ? How does this elucidate the proper interpretation of the fundamental nature of quantum physics?
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span id="High-energy_physics.2Fparticle_physics">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="High-energy_physics/particle_physics">
        High-energy physics/particle physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: High-energy physics/particle physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beyond_the_Standard_Model" title="Beyond the Standard Model">
        Beyond the Standard Model
       </a>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy_problem" title="Hierarchy problem">
         Hierarchy problem
        </a>
        : Why is
        <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">
         gravity
        </a>
        such a weak force? It becomes strong for particles only at the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planck_scale" title="Planck scale">
         Planck scale
        </a>
        , around 10
        <sup>
         19
        </sup>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GeV" title="GeV">
         GeV
        </a>
        , much above the
        <a href="/wiki/Electroweak_scale" title="Electroweak scale">
         electroweak scale
        </a>
        (100 GeV, the energy scale dominating physics at low energies). Why are these scales so different from each other? What prevents quantities at the electroweak scale, such as the
        <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">
         Higgs boson
        </a>
        mass, from getting
        <a href="/wiki/Renormalization" title="Renormalization">
         quantum corrections
        </a>
        on the order of the Planck scale? Is the solution
        <a href="/wiki/Supersymmetry" title="Supersymmetry">
         supersymmetry
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Extra_dimensions" title="Extra dimensions">
         extra dimensions
        </a>
        , or just
        <a href="/wiki/Anthropic_principle" title="Anthropic principle">
         anthropic
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Fine-tuned_Universe" title="Fine-tuned Universe">
         fine-tuning
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Planck_particle" title="Planck particle">
         Planck particle
        </a>
        : The Planck mass plays an important role in parts of mathematical physics. A series of researchers have suggested the existence of a fundamental particle with mass equal to or close to that of the Planck mass. The Planck mass is however enormous compared to any detected particle even compared to the Higgs particle. It is still an unsolved problem if there exist or even have existed a particle with close to the Planck mass. This is indirectly related to the hierarchy problem.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_monopole" title="Magnetic monopole">
         Magnetic monopoles
        </a>
        : Did particles that carry "magnetic charge" exist in some past, higher-energy epoch? If so, do any remain today? (
        <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dirac" title="Paul Dirac">
         Paul Dirac
        </a>
        showed the existence of some types of magnetic monopoles would explain
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charge_quantization" title="Charge quantization">
         charge quantization
        </a>
        .)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
         <a href="#cite_note-24">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Proton_decay" title="Proton decay">
         Proton decay
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Proton_spin_crisis" title="Proton spin crisis">
         spin crisis
        </a>
        : Is the proton fundamentally stable? Or does it decay with a finite lifetime as predicted by some extensions to the standard model?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-li-proton2011_25-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-li-proton2011-25">
          [25]
         </a>
        </sup>
        How do the quarks and gluons carry the spin of protons?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hansson2010_26-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-hansson2010-26">
          [26]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Supersymmetry" title="Supersymmetry">
         Supersymmetry
        </a>
        : Is spacetime supersymmetry realized at TeV scale? If so, what is the mechanism of supersymmetry breaking? Does supersymmetry stabilize the electroweak scale, preventing high quantum corrections? Does the lightest
        <a href="/wiki/Superpartner" title="Superpartner">
         supersymmetric particle
        </a>
        (LSP or
        <a href="/wiki/Lightest_Supersymmetric_Particle" title="Lightest Supersymmetric Particle">
         Lightest Supersymmetric Particle
        </a>
        ) comprise
        <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">
         dark matter
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Generation_(particle_physics)" title="Generation (particle physics)">
         Generations of matter
        </a>
        : Why are there three generations of
        <a href="/wiki/Quark" title="Quark">
         quarks
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Lepton" title="Lepton">
         leptons
        </a>
        ? Is there a theory that can explain the masses of particular quarks and leptons in particular generations from first principles (a theory of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yukawa_coupling" title="Yukawa coupling">
         Yukawa couplings
        </a>
        )?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlumhoferHutter1997_27-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-BlumhoferHutter1997-27">
          [27]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrino_mass" title="Neutrino mass">
         Neutrino mass
        </a>
        : What is the mass of neutrinos, whether they follow
        <a href="/wiki/Fermi%E2%80%93Dirac_statistics" title="Fermi–Dirac statistics">
         Dirac
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Majorana_fermion" title="Majorana fermion">
         Majorana
        </a>
        statistics? Is the mass hierarchy normal or inverted? Is the CP violating phase equal to 0?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ino-tifr_28-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ino-tifr-28">
          [28]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
         <a href="#cite_note-29">
          [29]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Color_confinement" title="Color confinement">
         Colour confinement
        </a>
        : Why has there never been measured a free quark or gluon, but only objects that are built out of them, such as
        <a href="/wiki/Meson" title="Meson">
         mesons
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Baryon" title="Baryon">
         baryons
        </a>
        ? How does this phenomenon emerge from
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_chromodynamics" title="Quantum chromodynamics">
         QCD
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Strong_CP_problem" title="Strong CP problem">
         Strong CP problem
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Axion" title="Axion">
         axions
        </a>
        : Why is the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strong_nuclear_interaction" title="Strong nuclear interaction">
         strong nuclear interaction
        </a>
        invariant to
        <a href="/wiki/Parity_(physics)" title="Parity (physics)">
         parity
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charge_conjugation" title="Charge conjugation">
         charge conjugation
        </a>
        ? Is
        <a href="/wiki/Peccei%E2%80%93Quinn_theory" title="Peccei–Quinn theory">
         Peccei–Quinn theory
        </a>
        the solution to this problem? Could axions be the main component of
        <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">
         dark matter
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Anomalous_magnetic_dipole_moment" title="Anomalous magnetic dipole moment">
         Anomalous magnetic dipole moment
        </a>
        : Why is the experimentally measured value of the
        <a href="/wiki/Muon" title="Muon">
         muon
        </a>
        's anomalous magnetic dipole moment ("muon g−2") significantly different from the theoretically predicted value of that physical constant?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
         <a href="#cite_note-30">
          [30]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Proton_radius_puzzle" title="Proton radius puzzle">
         Proton radius puzzle
        </a>
        : What is the electric
        <a href="/wiki/Charge_radius" title="Charge radius">
         charge radius
        </a>
        of the proton? How does it differ from gluonic charge?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Pentaquark" title="Pentaquark">
         Pentaquarks
        </a>
        and other
        <a href="/wiki/Exotic_hadron" title="Exotic hadron">
         exotic hadrons
        </a>
        : What combinations of quarks are possible? Why were pentaquarks so difficult to discover?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewScientist2003_31-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NewScientist2003-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Are they a tightly-bound system of five elementary particles, or a more weakly-bound pairing of a baryon and a meson?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewScientist2015_32-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NewScientist2015-32">
          [32]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mu_problem" title="Mu problem">
         Mu problem
        </a>
        : problem of
        <a href="/wiki/Supersymmetry" title="Supersymmetry">
         supersymmetric
        </a>
        theories, concerned with understanding the parameters of the theory.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Koide_formula" title="Koide formula">
         Koide formula
        </a>
        : An aspect of the
        <a href="/wiki/Generation_(particle_physics)" title="Generation (particle physics)">
         problem of particle generations
        </a>
        . The sum of the masses of the three charged leptons, divided by the square of the sum of the roots of these masses is
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\textstyle Q={\frac {2}{3}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               Q
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\textstyle Q={\frac {2}{3}}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\textstyle Q={\frac {2}{3}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1e176469393928f6707af31a0ad88a0c3b102d47" style="vertical-align: -1.338ex; width:6.595ex; height:3.676ex;"/>
        </span>
        , to within one standard deviation of observations. It is unknown how such a simple value comes about, and why it is the exact arithmetic average of the possible extreme values of 1/3 (equal masses) and 1 (one mass dominates).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Astronomy_and_astrophysics">
        Astronomy and astrophysics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Astronomy and astrophysics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Astrophysical_jet" title="Astrophysical jet">
         Astrophysical jet
        </a>
        : Why do only certain
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accretion_disc" title="Accretion disc">
         accretion discs
        </a>
        surrounding certain astronomical objects emit
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relativistic_jet" title="Relativistic jet">
         relativistic jets
        </a>
        along their polar axes? Why are there
        <a href="/wiki/Quasi-periodic_oscillation" title="Quasi-periodic oscillation">
         quasi-periodic oscillations
        </a>
        in many accretion discs?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
         <a href="#cite_note-33">
          [33]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Why does the period of these oscillations scale as the inverse of the mass of the central object?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
         <a href="#cite_note-34">
          [34]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Why are there sometimes overtones, and why do these appear at different frequency ratios in different objects?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
         <a href="#cite_note-35">
          [35]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diffuse_interstellar_band" title="Diffuse interstellar band">
         Diffuse interstellar bands
        </a>
        : What is responsible for the numerous interstellar absorption lines detected in astronomical spectra? Are they molecular in origin, and if so which molecules are responsible for them? How do they form?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Supermassive_black_hole" title="Supermassive black hole">
         Supermassive black holes
        </a>
        : What is the origin of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M-sigma_relation" title="M-sigma relation">
         M-sigma relation
        </a>
        between supermassive black hole mass and galaxy velocity dispersion?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
         <a href="#cite_note-36">
          [36]
         </a>
        </sup>
        How did the most distant
        <a href="/wiki/Quasar" title="Quasar">
         quasars
        </a>
        grow their supermassive black holes up to 10
        <sup>
         10
        </sup>
        solar masses so early in the history of the universe?
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GalacticRotation2.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="150" data-file-width="250" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/GalacticRotation2.svg/250px-GalacticRotation2.svg.png" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         Rotation curve of a typical spiral galaxy: predicted (
         <b>
          A
         </b>
         ) and observed (
         <b>
          B
         </b>
         ). Can the discrepancy between the curves be attributed to dark matter?
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuiper_cliff" title="Kuiper cliff">
         Kuiper cliff
        </a>
        : Why does the number of objects in the Solar System's
        <a href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt" title="Kuiper belt">
         Kuiper belt
        </a>
        fall off rapidly and unexpectedly beyond a radius of 50 astronomical units?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Flyby_anomaly" title="Flyby anomaly">
         Flyby anomaly
        </a>
        : Why is the observed energy of satellites
        <a href="/wiki/Gravity_assist" title="Gravity assist">
         flying by Earth
        </a>
        sometimes different by a minute amount from the value predicted by theory?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxy_rotation_problem" title="Galaxy rotation problem">
         Galaxy rotation problem
        </a>
        : Is
        <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">
         dark matter
        </a>
        responsible for differences in observed and theoretical speed of stars revolving around the centre of galaxies, or is it something else?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">
         Supernovae
        </a>
        : What is the exact mechanism by which an implosion of a dying star becomes an explosion?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/P-nuclei" title="P-nuclei">
         p-nuclei
        </a>
        : What astrophysical process is responsible for the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nucleogenesis" title="Nucleogenesis">
         nucleogenesis
        </a>
        of these rare isotopes?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ultra-high-energy_cosmic_ray" title="Ultra-high-energy cosmic ray">
         Ultra-high-energy cosmic ray
        </a>
        :
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newscientist_17-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-newscientist-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Why is it that some cosmic rays appear to possess energies that are impossibly high, given that there are no sufficiently energetic cosmic ray sources near the Earth? Why is it that (apparently) some cosmic rays emitted by distant sources have energies above the
        <a href="/wiki/Greisen%E2%80%93Zatsepin%E2%80%93Kuzmin_limit" title="Greisen–Zatsepin–Kuzmin limit">
         Greisen–Zatsepin–Kuzmin limit
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newscientist_17-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-newscientist-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Rotation rate of
        <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
         Saturn
        </a>
        : Why does the
        <a href="/wiki/Magnetosphere_of_Saturn" title="Magnetosphere of Saturn">
         magnetosphere of Saturn
        </a>
        exhibit a (slowly changing) periodicity close to that at which the planet's clouds rotate? What is the true rotation rate of Saturn's deep interior?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
         <a href="#cite_note-37">
          [37]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Origin of
        <a href="/wiki/Magnetar#Magnetic_field" title="Magnetar">
         magnetar magnetic field
        </a>
        : What is the origin of
        <a href="/wiki/Magnetar" title="Magnetar">
         magnetar
        </a>
        magnetic field?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecliptic_alignment_of_CMB_anisotropy" title="Ecliptic alignment of CMB anisotropy">
         Large-scale anisotropy
        </a>
        : Is the universe at very large scales
        <a href="/wiki/Anisotropy" title="Anisotropy">
         anisotropic
        </a>
        , making the
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmological_principle" title="Cosmological principle">
         cosmological principle
        </a>
        an invalid assumption? The number count and intensity dipole anisotropy in radio, NRAO VLA Sky Survey (NVSS) catalogue
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
         <a href="#cite_note-38">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
        is inconsistent with the local motion as derived from
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_microwave_background" title="Cosmic microwave background">
         cosmic microwave background
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
         <a href="#cite_note-39">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
         <a href="#cite_note-40">
          [40]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and indicate an intrinsic dipole anisotropy. The same NVSS radio data also shows an intrinsic dipole in polarization density and degree of polarization
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
         <a href="#cite_note-41">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
        in the same direction as in number count and intensity. There are other several observation revealing large-scale anisotropy. The optical polarization from quasars shows polarization alignment over a very large scale of Gpc.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
         <a href="#cite_note-42">
          [42]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
         <a href="#cite_note-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
         <a href="#cite_note-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The cosmic-microwave-background data shows several features of anisotropy,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
         <a href="#cite_note-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
         <a href="#cite_note-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
         <a href="#cite_note-47">
          [47]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
         <a href="#cite_note-48">
          [48]
         </a>
        </sup>
        which are not consistent with the
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">
         Big Bang
        </a>
        model.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_roar" title="Space roar">
         Space roar
        </a>
        : Why is space roar six times louder than expected? What is the source of space roar?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Age%E2%80%93metallicity_relation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Age–metallicity relation (page does not exist)">
         Age–metallicity relation
        </a>
        in the Galactic disk: Is there a universal age–metallicity relation (AMR) in the Galactic disk (both "thin" and "thick" parts of the disk)? Although in the local (primarily thin) disk of the
        <a href="/wiki/Milky_Way" title="Milky Way">
         Milky Way
        </a>
        there is no evidence of a strong AMR,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
         <a href="#cite_note-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
        a sample of 229 nearby "thick" disk stars has been used to investigate the existence of an age–metallicity relation in the Galactic thick disk, and indicate that there is an age–metallicity relation present in the thick disk.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
         <a href="#cite_note-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
         <a href="#cite_note-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Stellar ages from asteroseismology confirm the lack of any strong age-metallicity relation in the Galactic disc.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
         <a href="#cite_note-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang_nucleosynthesis" title="Big Bang nucleosynthesis">
         The lithium problem
        </a>
        : Why is there a discrepancy between the amount of lithium-7 predicted to be produced in
        <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang_nucleosynthesis" title="Big Bang nucleosynthesis">
         Big Bang nucleosynthesis
        </a>
        and the amount observed in very old stars?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
         <a href="#cite_note-53">
          [53]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/M82_X-2" title="M82 X-2">
         Ultraluminous pulsar
        </a>
        : The
        <a href="/wiki/Ultraluminous_X-ray_source" title="Ultraluminous X-ray source">
         ultraluminous X-ray source
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/M82_X-2" title="M82 X-2">
         M82 X-2
        </a>
        was thought to be a black hole, but in October 2014 data from NASA's space-based X-ray telescope
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NuStar" title="NuStar">
         NuStar
        </a>
        indicated that M82 X-2 is a
        <a href="/wiki/Pulsar" title="Pulsar">
         pulsar
        </a>
        many times brighter than the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eddington_limit" title="Eddington limit">
         Eddington limit
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fast_radio_burst" title="Fast radio burst">
         Fast radio bursts
        </a>
        : Transient radio pulses lasting only a few milliseconds, from emission regions thought to be no larger than a few hundred kilometres, and estimated to occur several hundred times a day. While several theories have been proposed, there is no generally accepted explanation for them. The only known
        <i>
         repeating
        </i>
        FRB emanates from a galaxy roughly 3 billion light years from Earth.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
         <a href="#cite_note-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
         <a href="#cite_note-55">
          [55]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Nature of
        <a href="/wiki/KIC_8462852" title="KIC 8462852">
         KIC 8462852
        </a>
        , commonly known as Tabby's Star: What is the origin of unusual
        <a href="/wiki/Luminosity" title="Luminosity">
         luminosity
        </a>
        changes of this star?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fermi_paradox" title="Fermi paradox">
         Fermi paradox
        </a>
        : Do extraterrestrial civilizations exist? If so, why do we not see them?
       </li>
       <li>
        Nature of
        <a href="/wiki/Wow!_signal" title="Wow! signal">
         Wow! signal
        </a>
        : Was that a real signal and, if so, what is the origin of it?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
         <a href="#cite_note-56">
          [56]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planetary_systems" title="Planetary systems">
         Planetary systems
        </a>
        : How does
        <a href="/wiki/Accretion_(astrophysics)" title="Accretion (astrophysics)">
         accretion
        </a>
        form planetary systems?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carnegie_57-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-carnegie-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Where did
        <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
         Earth
        </a>
        's water come from?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carnegie_57-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-carnegie-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_physics">
        Nuclear physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Nuclear physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Island-of-Stability.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="382" data-file-width="838" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Island-of-Stability.png/230px-Island-of-Stability.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Island-of-Stability.png/345px-Island-of-Stability.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Island-of-Stability.png/460px-Island-of-Stability.png 2x" width="230"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Island-of-Stability.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The "
         <a href="/wiki/Island_of_stability" title="Island of stability">
          island of stability
         </a>
         " in the proton vs. neutron number plot for heavy nuclei
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_chromodynamics" title="Quantum chromodynamics">
         Quantum chromodynamics
        </a>
        : What are the phases of strongly interacting matter, and what roles do they play in the evolution of
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmos" title="Cosmos">
         cosmos
        </a>
        ? What is the detailed
        <a href="/wiki/Parton_(particle_physics)" title="Parton (particle physics)">
         partonic
        </a>
        structure of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nucleons" title="Nucleons">
         nucleons
        </a>
        ? What does QCD predict for the properties of strongly interacting matter? What determines the key features of QCD, and what is their relation to the nature of
        <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">
         gravity
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Spacetime" title="Spacetime">
         spacetime
        </a>
        ? Do
        <a href="/wiki/Glueball" title="Glueball">
         glueballs
        </a>
        exist? Do
        <a href="/wiki/Gluon" title="Gluon">
         gluons
        </a>
        acquire mass dynamically despite having a zero
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rest_mass" title="Rest mass">
         rest mass
        </a>
        , within
        <a href="/wiki/Hadron" title="Hadron">
         hadrons
        </a>
        ? Does QCD truly lack
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CP-violation" title="CP-violation">
         CP-violations
        </a>
        ? Do gluons saturate when their occupation number is large? Do gluons form a dense system called
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Color_Glass_Condensate" title="Color Glass Condensate">
         Colour Glass Condensate
        </a>
        ? What are the signatures and evidences for the Balitsky-Fadin-Kuarev-
        <a href="/wiki/Lev_Lipatov" title="Lev Lipatov">
         Lipatov
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Balitsky-Kovchegov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Balitsky-Kovchegov (page does not exist)">
         Balitsky-Kovchegov
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Catani-Ciafaloni-Fiorani-Marchesini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Catani-Ciafaloni-Fiorani-Marchesini (page does not exist)">
         Catani-Ciafaloni-Fiorani-Marchesini
        </a>
        evolution equations?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Atomic_nucleus" title="Atomic nucleus">
         Nuclei
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_astrophysics" title="Nuclear astrophysics">
         nuclear astrophysics
        </a>
        : What is the nature of the
        <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_force" title="Nuclear force">
         nuclear force
        </a>
        that binds
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protons" title="Protons">
         protons
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrons" title="Neutrons">
         neutrons
        </a>
        into
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stable_isotope" title="Stable isotope">
         stable nuclei
        </a>
        and rare isotopes? What is the nature of exotic excitations in nuclei at the frontiers of stability and their role in stellar processes? What is the nature of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutron_stars" title="Neutron stars">
         neutron stars
        </a>
        and dense
        <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_matter" title="Nuclear matter">
         nuclear matter
        </a>
        ? What is the origin of the elements in the
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmos" title="Cosmos">
         cosmos
        </a>
        ? What are the nuclear reactions that drive
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stars" title="Stars">
         stars
        </a>
        and stellar explosions?
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span id="Atomic.2C_molecular_and_optical_physics">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Atomic,_molecular_and_optical_physics">
        Atomic, molecular and optical physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Atomic, molecular and optical physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Abraham%E2%80%93Minkowski_controversy" title="Abraham–Minkowski controversy">
         Abraham–Minkowski controversy
        </a>
        : What is the momentum of light in optical media?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensation" title="Bose–Einstein condensation">
         Bose–Einstein condensation
        </a>
        : How do we rigorously prove the existence of Bose–Einstein condensates for general interacting systems?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schlein-BEC_58-0">

          [58]
         </a>
        </sup>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_mechanics">
        Classical mechanics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Classical mechanics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Singular trajectories in the
        <a href="/wiki/Newtonian_dynamics" title="Newtonian dynamics">
         Newtonian
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/N-body_problem" title="N-body problem">
         <i>
          N
         </i>
         -body problem
        </a>
        : Does the set of initial conditions for which particles that undergo near-collisions gain infinite speed in finite time have
        <a href="/wiki/Measure_(mathematics)" title="Measure (mathematics)">
         measure
        </a>
        zero? This is known to be the case when
        <i>
         N
        </i>
        ≤ 4, but the question remains open for larger
        <i>
         N
        </i>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
         <a href="#cite_note-59">
          [59]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
         <a href="#cite_note-60">
          [60]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Condensed_matter_physics">
        Condensed matter physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Condensed matter physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BI2223-piece3_001.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="355" data-file-width="400" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/BI2223-piece3_001.jpg/150px-BI2223-piece3_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/BI2223-piece3_001.jpg/225px-BI2223-piece3_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/BI2223-piece3_001.jpg/300px-BI2223-piece3_001.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BI2223-piece3_001.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A sample of a
         <a href="/wiki/Cuprate_superconductor" title="Cuprate superconductor">
          cuprate superconductor
         </a>
         (specifically
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BSCCO" title="BSCCO">
          BSCCO
         </a>
         ). The mechanism for superconductivity of these materials is unknown.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-temperature_superconductor" title="High-temperature superconductor">
         High-temperature superconductors
        </a>
        : What is the mechanism that causes certain materials to exhibit
        <a href="/wiki/Superconductivity" title="Superconductivity">
         superconductivity
        </a>
        at temperatures much higher than around 25
        <a href="/wiki/Kelvin" title="Kelvin">
         kelvin
        </a>
        ? Is it possible to make a material that is a superconductor at room temperature?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Amorphous_solid" title="Amorphous solid">
         Amorphous solids
        </a>
        : What is the nature of the
        <a href="/wiki/Glass_transition" title="Glass transition">
         glass transition
        </a>
        between a fluid or regular solid and a glassy
        <a href="/wiki/Phase_(matter)" title="Phase (matter)">
         phase
        </a>
        ? What are the physical processes giving rise to the general properties of glasses and the glass transition?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
         <a href="#cite_note-61">
          [61]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
         <a href="#cite_note-62">
          [62]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cryogenic_electron_emission&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cryogenic electron emission (page does not exist)">
         Cryogenic electron emission
        </a>
        : Why does the electron emission in the absence of light increase as the temperature of a
        <a href="/wiki/Photomultiplier" title="Photomultiplier">
         photomultiplier
        </a>
        is decreased?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
         <a href="#cite_note-63">
          [63]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
         <a href="#cite_note-64">
          [64]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Sonoluminescence" title="Sonoluminescence">
         Sonoluminescence
        </a>
        : What causes the emission of short bursts of light from imploding bubbles in a liquid when excited by sound?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
         <a href="#cite_note-65">
          [65]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
         <a href="#cite_note-66">
          [66]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         Turbulence
        </a>
        : Is it possible to make a theoretical model to describe the statistics of a turbulent flow (in particular, its internal structures)?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Also, under what conditions do
        <a href="/wiki/Navier%E2%80%93Stokes_existence_and_smoothness" title="Navier–Stokes existence and smoothness">
         smooth solutions to the Navier–Stokes equations
        </a>
        exist? This problem is also listed as one of the
        <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Prize_Problems" title="Millennium Prize Problems">
         Millennium Prize Problems
        </a>
        in mathematics.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alfv%C3%A9nic_turbulence&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alfvénic turbulence (page does not exist)">
         Alfvénic turbulence
        </a>
        : In the solar wind and the turbulence in solar flares, coronal mass ejections, and magnetospheric substorms are major unsolved problems in space plasma physics.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
         <a href="#cite_note-67">
          [67]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Topological_order" title="Topological order">
         Topological order
        </a>
        : Is topological order stable at non-zero
        <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
         temperature
        </a>
        ? Equivalently, is it possible to have three-dimensional
        <a href="/wiki/Stabilizer_code" title="Stabilizer code">
         self-correcting
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Qubit" title="Qubit">
         quantum memory
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yoshida_68-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-yoshida-68">
          [68]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fractional_Hall_effect" title="Fractional Hall effect">
         Fractional Hall effect
        </a>
        : What mechanism explains the existence of the
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle u=5/2}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               u
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               5
              </mn>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mo>
                /
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <mn>
               2
              </mn>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle u=5/2}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle u=5/2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7e6cf610862620b1f80d912258f14236a51a034b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:7.916ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
        </span>
        state in the fractional
        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_Hall_effect" title="Quantum Hall effect">
         quantum Hall effect
        </a>
        ? Does it describe quasiparticles with
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fractional_statistics#Non-abelian_anyons" title="Fractional statistics">
         non-Abelian fractional statistics
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
         <a href="#cite_note-69">
          [69]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tright">

         <span class="mwe-math-element">
          <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

         </span>

      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Liquid_crystal" title="Liquid crystal">
         Liquid crystals
        </a>
        : Can the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nematic" title="Nematic">
         nematic
        </a>
        to
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smectic" title="Smectic">
         smectic
        </a>
        (A) phase transition in liquid crystal states be characterized as a
        <a href="/wiki/Background_independence" title="Background independence">
         universal
        </a>
        phase transition?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mukherjee-liqcryst_70-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-mukherjee-liqcryst-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yethiraj-liqcryst_71-0">

         </a>
