       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semiconductor_nanocrystal" title="Semiconductor nanocrystal">
         Semiconductor nanocrystals
        </a>
        : What is the cause of the nonparabolicity of the energy-size dependence for the lowest
        <a href="/wiki/Absorption_(electromagnetic_radiation)" title="Absorption (electromagnetic radiation)">
         optical absorption transition
        </a>
        of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quantum_dots" title="Quantum dots">
         quantum dots
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norris-electronic_72-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-norris-electronic-72">
          [72]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Whisker_(metallurgy)" title="Whisker (metallurgy)">
         Whisker (metallurgy)
        </a>
        : In electrical devices, some metallic surfaces may spontaneously grow fine metallic whiskers, which can lead to equipment failures. While compressive mechanical stress is known to encourage whisker formation, the growth mechanism has yet to be determined.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plasma_physics">
        Plasma physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Plasma physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Plasma_(physics)" title="Plasma (physics)">
         Plasma physics
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Fusion_power" title="Fusion power">
         fusion power
        </a>
        : Fusion energy may potentially provide power from abundant resource (e.g. hydrogen) without the type of radioactive waste that fission energy currently produces. However, can ionized gases (plasma) be
        <a href="/wiki/Tokamak" title="Tokamak">
         confined
        </a>
        long enough and at a high enough temperature to create fusion power? What is the physical origin of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H-mode" title="H-mode">
         H-mode
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
         <a href="#cite_note-73">
          [73]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_cycle" title="Solar cycle">
         Solar cycle
        </a>
        :How does the Sun generate its periodically reversing large-scale magnetic field? How do other solar-like stars generate their magnetic fields, and what are the similarities and differences between stellar activity cycles and that of the Sun?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
         <a href="#cite_note-74">
          [74]
         </a>
        </sup>
        What caused the
        <a href="/wiki/Maunder_Minimum" title="Maunder Minimum">
         Maunder Minimum
        </a>
        and other grand minima, and how does the solar cycle recover from a minima state?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coronal_heating_problem" title="Coronal heating problem">
         Coronal heating problem
        </a>
        : Why is the Sun's corona (atmosphere layer) so much hotter than the Sun's surface? Why is the
        <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_reconnection" title="Magnetic reconnection">
         magnetic reconnection
        </a>
        effect many orders of magnitude faster than predicted by standard models?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fermi_acceleration#The_injection_problem" title="Fermi acceleration">
         The injection problem
        </a>
        :
        <a href="/wiki/Fermi_acceleration" title="Fermi acceleration">
         Fermi acceleration
        </a>
        is thought to be the primary mechanism that accelerates astrophysical particles to high energy. However, it is unclear what mechanism causes those particles to initially have energies high enough for Fermi acceleration to work on them.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
         <a href="#cite_note-75">
          [75]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/C/2006_P1#Ulysses_probe" title="C/2006 P1">
         Solar wind interaction with comets
        </a>
        : In 2007 the
        <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_(spacecraft)" title="Ulysses (spacecraft)">
         <i>
          Ulysses
         </i>
         spacecraft
        </a>
        passed through the tail of comet
        <a href="/wiki/C/2006_P1" title="C/2006 P1">
         C/2006 P1
        </a>
        (McNaught) and found surprising results concerning the interaction of the solar wind with the tail.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biophysics">
        Biophysics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Biophysics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Stochastic_process" title="Stochastic process">
         Stochasticity
        </a>
        and robustness to
        <a href="/wiki/Signal-to-noise_ratio" title="Signal-to-noise ratio">
         noise
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Gene_expression" title="Gene expression">
         gene expression
        </a>
        : How do genes govern our body, withstanding different external pressures and internal stochasticity?
        <a href="/wiki/Gene_regulatory_network" title="Gene regulatory network">
         Certain models
        </a>
        exist for genetic processes, but we are far from understanding the whole picture, in particular in
        <a href="/wiki/Morphogenesis" title="Morphogenesis">
         development
        </a>
        where gene expression must be tightly regulated.
       </li>
       <li>
        Quantitative study of the
        <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">
         immune system
        </a>
        : What are the quantitative properties of immune responses? What are the basic building blocks of immune system networks?
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Unified_brain_processing_theory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Unified brain processing theory (page does not exist)">
         Unified brain processing theory
        </a>
        : How to unify
        <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">
         physics
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">
         neuroscience
        </a>
        ?
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VandenNoort2016_76-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-VandenNoort2016-76">
          [76]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Homochirality" title="Homochirality">
         Homochirality
        </a>
        : What is the origin of the preponderance of specific
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enantiomers" title="Enantiomers">
         enantiomers
        </a>
        in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biochemical_system" title="Biochemical system">
         biochemical systems
        </a>
        ?
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Problems_solved_in_recent_decades">
        Problems solved in recent decades
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unsolved_problems_in_physics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Problems solved in recent decades">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Origin of short
        <a href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_burst" title="Gamma-ray burst">
         gamma-ray burst
        </a>
        (1993
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_77-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-77">
          [77]
         </a>
        </sup>
        -2017): From binary
        <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star" title="Neutron star">
         neutron stars
        </a>
        merger, produce a
        <a href="/wiki/Kilonova" title="Kilonova">
         kilonova
        </a>
        explosion and short gamma-ray burst
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GRB_170817A" title="GRB 170817A">
         GRB 170817A
        </a>
        was detected in both
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_wave" title="Electromagnetic wave">
         electromagnetic waves
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_wave" title="Gravitational wave">
         gravitational wave
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/GW170817" title="GW170817">
         GW170817
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SM-20171016_78-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-SM-20171016-78">
          [78]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20170825_79-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NAT-20170825-79">
          [79]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Missing_baryon_problem" title="Missing baryon problem">
         Missing baryon problem
        </a>
        (1998
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
         <a href="#cite_note-80">
          [80]
         </a>
        </sup>
        -2017): proclaimed solved in October 2017, with the missing baryons located in hot intergalactic gas.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
         <a href="#cite_note-81">
          [81]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Existence of
        <a href="/wiki/Time_crystal" title="Time crystal">
         time crystals
        </a>
        (2012–2016): In 2016, the idea of time-crystals was proposed by two groups independently Khemani et al.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
         <a href="#cite_note-82">
          [82]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and Else et al.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
         <a href="#cite_note-83">
          [83]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Both of these groups showed that in small systems which are disordered and periodic in time, one can observe the phenomenon of time crystals. Norman Yao et al. extended the calculations for a model (which has the same qualitative features) in the laboratory environment. This was then used by two teams, a group led by
        <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Monroe" title="Christopher Monroe">
         Christopher Monroe
        </a>
        at the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland" title="University of Maryland">
         University of Maryland
        </a>
        and a group led by
        <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lukin" title="Mikhail Lukin">
         Mikhail Lukin
        </a>
        at
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harvard_university" title="Harvard university">
         Harvard university
        </a>
        , who were both able to show evidence for time crystals in the lab-setting, showing that for short times the systems exhibited the dynamics similar to the predicted one.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monroe_84-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Monroe-84">
          [84]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lukin_85-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Lukin-85">
          [85]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Existence of
        <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_wave" title="Gravitational wave">
         gravitational waves
        </a>
        (1916–2016): On 11 February 2016, the
        <a href="/wiki/LIGO" title="LIGO">
         Advanced LIGO
        </a>
        team announced that they had
        <a href="/wiki/First_observation_of_gravitational_waves" title="First observation of gravitational waves">
         directly detected gravitational waves
        </a>
        from a
        <a href="/wiki/Binary_black_hole" title="Binary black hole">
         pair
        </a>
        of black holes
        <a href="/wiki/Stellar_collision" title="Stellar collision">
         merging
        </a>
        ,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Discovery_2016_86-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Discovery_2016-86">
          [86]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abbot_87-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Abbot-87">
          [87]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NSF_88-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NSF-88">
          [88]
         </a>
        </sup>
        which was also the first detection of a stellar binary black hole.
       </li>
       <li>
        Perform a
        <a href="/wiki/Loopholes_in_Bell_test_experiments" title="Loopholes in Bell test experiments">
         loophole-free Bell test experiment
        </a>
        (1970
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pearle-1970_89-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Pearle-1970-89">
          [89]
         </a>
        </sup>
        –2015): In October 2015, scientists from the
        <a href="/wiki/Kavli_Institute_of_Nanoscience" title="Kavli Institute of Nanoscience">
         Kavli Institute of Nanoscience
        </a>
        reported that the failure of the local hidden-variable hypothesis is supported at the 96% confidence level based on a "loophole-free Bell test" study.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTR-20151021_90-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NTR-20151021-90">
          [90]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20151021_91-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151021-91">
          [91]
         </a>
        </sup>
        These results were confirmed by two studies with statistical significance over 5 standard deviations which were published in December 2015.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRL115-250401_92-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-PRL115-250401-92">
          [92]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PRL115-250402_93-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-PRL115-250402-93">
          [93]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Existence of
        <a href="/wiki/Pentaquark" title="Pentaquark">
         pentaquarks
        </a>
        (1964–2015): In July 2015, the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LHCb" title="LHCb">
         LHCb
        </a>
        collaboration at
        <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">
         CERN
        </a>
        identified pentaquarks in the
        <span class="nowrap">
         Λ
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          0
          <br/>
          b
         </span>
         →J/ψK
         <sup>
          −
         </sup>
         p
        </span>
        channel, which represents the decay of the bottom lambda baryon
        <span class="nowrap">
         (Λ
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          0
          <br/>
          b
         </span>
         )
        </span>
        into a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J/%CF%88_meson" title="J/ψ meson">
         J/ψ meson
        </a>
        <span class="nowrap">
         (J/ψ)
        </span>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Kaon" title="Kaon">
         kaon
        </a>
        <span class="nowrap">
         (K
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          −
          <br/>
         </span>
         )
        </span>
        and a
        <a href="/wiki/Proton" title="Proton">
         proton
        </a>
        (p). The results showed that sometimes, instead of decaying directly into mesons and baryons, the
        <span class="nowrap">
         Λ
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          0
          <br/>
          b
         </span>
        </span>
        decayed via intermediate pentaquark states. The two states, named
        <span class="nowrap">
         P
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          +
          <br/>
          c
         </span>
         (4380)
        </span>
        and
        <span class="nowrap">
         P
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          +
          <br/>
          c
         </span>
         (4450)
        </span>
        , had individual
        <a href="/wiki/Statistical_significance" title="Statistical significance">
         statistical significances
        </a>
        of 9 σ and 12 σ, respectively, and a combined significance of 15 σ — enough to claim a formal discovery. The two pentaquark states were both observed decaying strongly to
        <span class="nowrap">
         J/ψp
        </span>
        , hence must have a valence quark content of two
        <a href="/wiki/Up_quark" title="Up quark">
         up quarks
        </a>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Down_quark" title="Down quark">
         down quark
        </a>
        , a
        <a href="/wiki/Charm_quark" title="Charm quark">
         charm quark
        </a>
        , and an anti-charm quark (
        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">
          <br/>
         </span>
         u
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">
          <br/>
         </span>
         u
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">
          <br/>
         </span>
         d
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">
          <br/>
         </span>
         c
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:right">
          <br/>
         </span>
         <span style="text-decoration:overline;">
          c
         </span>
         <span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:0.8em;line-height:1.0em;font-size:80%;text-align:left">
          <br/>
         </span>
        </span>
        ), making them
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charmonium" title="Charmonium">
         charmonium
        </a>
        -pentaquarks.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LHCb2015_94-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-LHCb2015-94">
          [94]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Photon_underproduction_crisis" title="Photon underproduction crisis">
         Photon underproduction crisis
        </a>
        (2014–2015): This problem was resolved by Khaire and Srianand.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
         <a href="#cite_note-95">
          [95]
         </a>
        </sup>
        They show that a factor 2 to 5 times large metagalactic photoionization rate can be easily obtained using updated quasar and galaxy observations. Recent observations of quasars indicate that the quasar contribution to ultraviolet photons is a factor of 2 larger than previous estimates. The revised galaxy contribution is a factor of 3 larger. These together solve the crisis.
       </li>
       <li>
        Existence of
        <a href="/wiki/Ball_lightning" title="Ball lightning">
         ball lightning
        </a>
        (1638
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
         <a href="#cite_note-96">
          [96]
         </a>
        </sup>
        –2014): In January 2014, scientists from
        <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Normal_University" title="Northwest Normal University">
         Northwest Normal University
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Lanzhou" title="Lanzhou">
         Lanzhou
        </a>
        , China, published the results of recordings made in July 2012 of the optical spectrum of what was thought to be natural ball lightning made during the study of ordinary cloud–ground lightning on China's
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qinghai_Plateau" title="Qinghai Plateau">
         Qinghai Plateau
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLspectrum_97-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-BLspectrum-97">
          [97]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLspectrumvideo_98-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-BLspectrumvideo-98">
          [98]
         </a>
        </sup>
        At a distance of 900 m (3,000 ft), a total of 1.3 seconds of digital video of the ball lightning and its spectrum was made, from the formation of the ball lightning after the ordinary lightning struck the ground, up to the optical decay of the phenomenon. The recorded ball lightning is believed to be vaporized soil elements that then rapidly oxidize in the atmosphere. The nature of the true theory is still not clear.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BLspectrumvideo_98-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-BLspectrumvideo-98">
          [98]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">
         Higgs boson
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electroweak_symmetry_breaking" title="Electroweak symmetry breaking">
         electroweak symmetry breaking
        </a>
        (1963
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MyLifeAsABoson_99-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-MyLifeAsABoson-99">
          [99]
         </a>
        </sup>
        –2012): The mechanism responsible for breaking the electroweak gauge symmetry, giving mass to the
        <a href="/wiki/W_and_Z_bosons" title="W and Z bosons">
         W and Z bosons
        </a>
        , was solved with the discovery of the
        <a href="/wiki/Higgs_boson" title="Higgs boson">
         Higgs boson
        </a>
        of the
        <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">
         Standard Model
        </a>
        , with the expected couplings to the weak bosons. No evidence of a strong dynamics solution, as proposed by
        <a href="/wiki/Technicolor_(physics)" title="Technicolor (physics)">
         technicolor
        </a>
        , has been observed.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hipparcos#The_Pleiades_distance_controversy" title="Hipparcos">
         Hipparcos anomaly
        </a>
        (1997
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
         <a href="#cite_note-100">
          [100]
         </a>
        </sup>
        –2012): The High Precision Parallax Collecting Satellite (Hipparcos) measured the parallax of the
        <a href="/wiki/Pleiades" title="Pleiades">
         Pleiades
        </a>
        and determined a
        <a href="/wiki/Pleiades#Distance" title="Pleiades">
         distance
        </a>
        of 385 light years. This was significantly different from other measurements made by means of actual to apparent brightness measurement or
        <a href="/wiki/Absolute_magnitude" title="Absolute magnitude">
         absolute magnitude
        </a>
        . The anomaly was due to the use of a weighted mean when there is a correlation between distances and distance errors for stars in clusters. It is resolved by using an unweighted mean. There is no systematic bias in the Hipparcos data when it comes to star clusters.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
         <a href="#cite_note-101">
          [101]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light_neutrino_anomaly" title="Faster-than-light neutrino anomaly">
         Faster-than-light neutrino anomaly
        </a>
        (2011–2012): In 2011, the
        <a href="/wiki/OPERA_experiment" title="OPERA experiment">
         OPERA experiment
        </a>
        mistakenly observed
        <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">
         neutrinos
        </a>
        appearing to travel
        <a href="/wiki/Faster-than-light" title="Faster-than-light">
         faster than light
        </a>
        . On July 12, 2012 OPERA updated their paper by including the new sources of errors in their calculations. They found agreement of neutrino speed with the speed of light.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-op4_102-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-op4-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_anomaly" title="Pioneer anomaly">
         Pioneer anomaly
        </a>
        (1980–2012): There was a deviation in the predicted accelerations of the
        <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_program" title="Pioneer program">
         Pioneer
        </a>
        spacecraft as they left the Solar System.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Open_Questions_4-6">
         <a href="#cite_note-Open_Questions-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newscientist_17-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-newscientist-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
        It is believed that this is a result of previously unaccounted-for
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermal_recoil_force" title="Thermal recoil force">
         thermal recoil force
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
         <a href="#cite_note-103">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
         <a href="#cite_note-104">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Numerical solution for
        <a href="/wiki/Binary_black_hole" title="Binary black hole">
         binary black hole
        </a>
        (1960s–2005): The numerical solution of the two body problem in general relativity was achieved after four decades of research. In 2005 (
        <a href="/wiki/Annus_mirabilis" title="Annus mirabilis">
         annus mirabilis
        </a>
        of numerical relativity) when three groups devised the breakthrough techniques.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breakthroughs_105-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-breakthroughs-105">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Long-duration
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_ray_bursts" title="Gamma ray bursts">
         gamma ray bursts
        </a>
        (1993
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_77-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-77">
          [77]
         </a>
        </sup>
        –2003): Long-duration bursts are associated with the deaths of massive stars in a specific kind of
        <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">
         supernova
        </a>
        -like event commonly referred to as a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypernova" title="Hypernova">
         collapsar
        </a>
        . However, there are also long-duration GRBs that show evidence against an associated supernova, such as the Swift event
        <a href="/wiki/GRB_060614" title="GRB 060614">
         GRB 060614
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_neutrino_problem" title="Solar neutrino problem">
         Solar neutrino problem
        </a>
        (1968
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
         <a href="#cite_note-106">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
        –2001): Solved by a new understanding of
        <a href="/wiki/Neutrino" title="Neutrino">
         neutrino
        </a>
        physics, requiring a modification of the
        <a href="/wiki/Standard_Model" title="Standard Model">
         Standard Model
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">
         particle physics
        </a>
        —specifically,
        <a href="/wiki/Neutrino_oscillation" title="Neutrino oscillation">
         neutrino oscillation
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Create
        <a href="/wiki/Bose%E2%80%93Einstein_condensate" title="Bose–Einstein condensate">
         Bose–Einstein condensate
        </a>
        (1924
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
         <a href="#cite_note-107">
          [107]
         </a>
        </sup>
        -1995): Composite bosons in the form of dilute atomic vapours were cooled to quantum degeneracy using the techniques of
        <a href="/wiki/Laser_cooling" title="Laser cooling">
         laser cooling
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Evaporative_cooling_(atomic_physics)" title="Evaporative cooling (atomic physics)">
         evaporative cooling
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_age_problem" title="Cosmic age problem">
         Cosmic age problem
        </a>
        (1920s-1990s): The estimated age of the universe was around 3 to 8 billion years younger than estimates of the ages of the oldest stars in the Milky Way. Better estimates for the distances to the stars, and the recognition of the accelerating expansion of the universe, reconciled the age estimates.
       </li>
       <li>
        Nature of
        <a href="/wiki/Quasar" title="Quasar">
         quasars
        </a>
        (1950s-1980s): The nature of quasars was not understood for decades.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quasar-jbo_108-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-quasar-jbo-108">
          [108]
         </a>
        </sup>
        They are now accepted as a type of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_galaxy" title="Active galaxy">
         active galaxy
        </a>
        where the enormous energy output results from matter falling into a massive
        <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">
         black hole
        </a>
        in the centre of the galaxy.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quasar-hubble_109-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-quasar-hubble-109">
          [109]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

          </b>
         </span>

           Hammond, Richard (May 1, 2008).
           <i>
            The Unknown Universe: The Origin of the Universe, Quantum Gravity, Wormholes, and Other Things Science Still Can't Explain
           </i>

         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation journal">
           Wang, Qingdi; Zhu, Zhen;
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Unruh" title="William Unruh">
            Unruh, William G.
           </a>
           (2017-05-11).
           <a class="external text" href="https://link.aps.org/doi/10.1103/PhysRevD.95.103504" rel="nofollow">
            "How the huge energy of quantum vacuum gravitates to drive the slow accelerating expansion of the Universe"
           </a>
           .
           <i>
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_Review_D" title="Physical Review D">
             Physical Review D
            </a>
           </i>
           .
           <b>
            95
           </b>
           (10): 103504.
           <a href="/wiki/ArXiv" title="ArXiv">

           </a>
           :
           <span class="plainlinks">
            <a class="external text" href="//arxiv.org/abs/1703.00543" rel="nofollow">
             1703.00543
            </a>
            <img alt="Freely accessible" data-file-height="813" data-file-width="512" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/9px-Lock-green.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/14px-Lock-green.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lock-green.svg/18px-Lock-green.svg.png 2x" title="Freely accessible" width="9"/>
           </span>
           .
           <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">
            doi
           </a>
           :
           <a class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1103%2FPhysRevD.95.103504" rel="nofollow">
            10.1103/PhysRevD.95.103504
           </a>
           .
           <q>
            This problem is widely regarded as one of the major obstacles to further progress in fundamental physics [...] Its importance has been emphasized by various authors from different aspects. For example, it has been described as a “veritable crisis” [...] and even “the mother of all physics problems” [...] While it might be possible that people working on a particular problem tend to emphasize or even exaggerate its importance, those authors all agree that this is a problem that needs to be solved, although there is little agreement on what is the right direction to find the solution.
           </q>

          </div>

        </tr>
